# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Platform Audit: Deprecated Struct Fields in Kubernetes API Types

## Your Task

Your platform team is inventorying deprecated API fields that are still defined in Kubernetes. Find all Go source files in `kubernetes/kubernetes` that define struct fields or constants with `Deprecated` in the identifier name (e.g., `DeprecatedServiceAccount`, `DeprecatedTopology`, `DeprecatedSource`).

## Scope

Search `staging/src/k8s.io/api/` and `pkg/apis/` directories. Include both the API types (staging) and internal types (pkg/apis). Also include the annotation constants file that defines deprecated annotation key constants.

**IMPORTANT**: Only include files that DEFINE the deprecated identifiers (struct field declarations or const declarations). Do not include files that merely reference or use these deprecated fields (e.g., conversion functions, deepcopy, tests).

## Context

You are performing a platform audit to inventory all deprecated but still-present API fields in Kubernetes. This is a prerequisite for planning deprecation removal timelines and assessing backward compatibility impact. The deprecated fields span core types (Pod, Container), discovery types (EndpointSlice), event types, and annotation constants.

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `kubernetes/kubernetes` at v1.32.0
- `etcd-io/etcd` at v3.5.17
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "kubernetes/kubernetes", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of deprecated fields found."
}
```

**Important**: Use `"kubernetes/kubernetes"` for the repo name. Strip `github.com/` prefix.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes`). Strip this prefix in your answer.

Include only the `files` field. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all files that define deprecated struct fields or constants?
- **Keyword presence**: Does your answer reference key deprecated identifiers (DeprecatedServiceAccount, DeprecatedTopology, DeprecatedSource, DeprecatedSeccompProfileDockerDefault)?

of the last change, of some Pod or Service object, that triggered the endpoints object change.\n98: \t// In other words, if a Pod / Service changed at time T0, that change was observed by endpoints\n99: \t// controller at T1, and the Endpoints object was changed at T2, the\n100: \t// EndpointsLastChangeTriggerTime would be set to T0.\n101: \t//\n102: \t// The \"endpoints change trigger\" here means any Pod or Service change that resulted in the\n103: \t// Endpoints object change.\n104: \t//\n105: \t// Given the definition of the \"endpoints change trigger\", please note that this annotation will\n106: \t// be set ONLY for endpoints object changes triggered by either Pod or Service change. If the\n107: \t// Endpoints object changes due to other reasons, this annotation won't be set (or updated if it's\n108: \t// already set).\n109: \t//\n110: \t// This annotation will be used to compute the in-cluster network programming latency SLI, see\n111: \t// https://github.com/kubernetes/community/blob/master/sig-scalability/slos/network_programming_latency.md\n112: \tEndpointsLastChangeTriggerTime = \"endpoints.kubernetes.io/last-change-trigger-time\"\n113: \n114: \t// EndpointsOverCapacity will be set on an Endpoints resource when it\n115: \t// exceeds the maximum capacity of 1000 addresses. Initially the Endpoints\n116: \t// controller will set this annotation with a value of \"warning\". In a\n117: \t// future release, the controller may set this annotation with a value of\n118: \t// \"truncated\" to indicate that any addresses exceeding the limit of 1000\n119: \t// have been truncated from the Endpoints resource.\n120: \tEndpointsOverCapacity = \"endpoints.kubernetes.io/over-capacity\"\n121: \n122: \t// MigratedPluginsAnnotationKey is the annotation key, set for CSINode objects, that is a comma-separated\n123: \t// list of in-tree plugins that will be serviced by the CSI backend on the Node represented by CSINode.\n124: \t// This annotation is used by the Attach Detach Controller to determine whether to use the in-tree or\n125: \t// CSI Backend for a volume plugin on a specific node.\n126: \tMigratedPluginsAnnotationKey = \"storage.alpha.kubernetes.io/migrated-plugins\"\n127: \n128: \t// PodDeletionCost can be used to set to an int32 that represent the cost of deleting\n129: \t// a pod compared to other pods belonging to the same ReplicaSet. Pods with lower\n130: \t// deletion cost are preferred to be deleted before pods with higher deletion cost.\n131: \t// Note that this is honored on a best-effort basis, and so it does not offer guarantees on\n132: \t// pod deletion order.\n133: \t// The implicit deletion cost for pods that don't set the annotation is 0, negative values are permitted.\n134: \t//\n135: \t// This annotation is beta-level and is only honored when PodDeletionCost feature is enabled.\n136: \tPodDeletionCost = \"controller.kubernetes.io/pod-deletion-cost\"\n137: \n138: \t// DeprecatedAnnotationTopologyAwareHints can be used to enable or disable\n139: \t// Topology Aware Hints for a Service. This may be set to \"Auto\" or\n140: \t// \"Disabled\". Any other value is treated as \"Disabled\". This annotation has\n141: \t// been deprecated in favor of the `service.kubernetes.io/topology-mode`\n142: \t// annotation which also allows \"Auto\" and \"Disabled\", but is not limited to\n143: \t// those (it's open ended to provide room for experimentation while we\n144: \t// pursue configuration for topology via specification). When both\n145: \t// `service.kubernetes.io/topology-aware-hints` and\n146: \t// `service.kubernetes.io/topology-mode` annotations are set, the value of\n147: \t// `service.kubernetes.io/topology-aware-hints` has precedence.\n148: \tDeprecatedAnnotationTopologyAwareHints = \"service.kubernetes.io/topology-aware-hints\"\n149: \n150: \t// AnnotationTopologyMode can be used to enable or disable Topology Aware\n151: \t// Routing for a Service. Well known values are \"Auto\" and \"Disabled\".\n152: \t// Implementations may choose to develop new topology approaches, exposing\n153: \t// them with domain-prefixed values. For example, \"example.com/lowest-rtt\"\n154: \t// could be a valid implementation-specific value for this annotation. These\n155: \t// heuristics will often populate topology hints on EndpointSlices, but that\n156: \t// is not a requirement.\n157: \tAnnotationTopologyMode = \"service.kubernetes.io/topology-mode\"\n158: )\n159: ",
